Working With Time...¶

https://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/user_guide/timeseries.html¶

In [10]:
import datetime # import the datetime library

There are three major ways you can deal with time in Pandas:¶

  1. Timestamps (DatetimeIndex, datetime64)
  2. Periods / Timespans (PeriodIndex, period[freq])
  3. Timedeltas (TimedeltaIndex, timedelta64)
In [11]:
# timestamps 

timestamps = pd.Timestamp(datetime.datetime(2019, 5, 9))
timestamps
Out[11]:
Timestamp('2019-05-09 00:00:00')
In [12]:
# periods

periods = pd.Series(pd.period_range('1/1/2019', freq='M', periods=3))
periods
Out[12]:
0    2019-01
1    2019-02
2    2019-03
dtype: period[M]

It's important to note that both timestamps and periods can serve as an index.¶

Remember, an index is a way to access a data point in a data frame.¶

In [13]:

Dummy Variables:¶

Often times, you will have Yes / No values, or categorical variables, that you need to transform into numerical data. The easiest way to do that is with dummy variables.

In [22]:
df.head()
Out[22]:
id company_size age sex clicked_on_ad ad_type location
timestamp
2000-12-25 19:59:20.273663 a85fd39a-5610-4619-92b4-d1bdd305414e large 51 M Yes Luxury Canada
2001-03-15 04:14:13.841541 2ecb87dc-ef9d-4eab-a28a-a4a0eb4ae951 large 92 N Yes Tech NorthEast
2001-03-13 04:33:44.346952 db4260d6-0bd9-4b5d-a3e7-1137784ef930 startup 65 M Yes Luxury NorthEast
2001-02-24 00:04:27.449789 1ca931d2-41b7-49ee-b8ec-1a3943fb1ad3 small 38 N No Political SouthEast
2000-11-22 23:13:36.186362 caabb63e-8d41-497b-ba75-aff80fe9649f small 82 M Yes Business NorthWest
In [23]:
df = pd.concat([df.drop('clicked_on_ad',axis=1),pd.get_dummies((df['clicked_on_ad'])).rename(columns = lambda x: 'clicked_on_ad' + str(x))],axis=1)
